# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain

## Your Task

Trace how LLVM IR types flow from the type creation API to code generation in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files implementing: the Type class hierarchy (IntegerType, FunctionType, StructType), the type system's context ownership, and the IR type to machine type lowering in SelectionDAG.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the LLVM IR type system and created a comprehensive answer document at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary

I traced the complete flow of LLVM IR types from creation to code generation:

### **Type Class Hierarchy**
- **Type.h**: Base Type class with TypeID enum covering primitive and derived types
- **DerivedTypes.h**: Concrete implementations of IntegerType, FunctionType, StructType, etc.

### **Type Context Ownership**
- **LLVMContext.h**: Public interface managing global type state
- **LLVMContextImpl.h**: Private implementation storing type uniquing tables (IntegerTypes, FunctionTypes, AnonStructTypes, NamedStructTypes, ArrayTypes, VectorTypes, PointerTypes)

### **Type to Code Generation Chain**
1. **IR Type Creation** → IntegerType::get(), FunctionType::get(), StructType::get/create() (Type.cpp)
2. **SelectionDAG Building** → SelectionDAGBuilder converts IR instructions to DAG nodes (SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp)
3. **Type Conversion** → TargetLowering::getValueType() converts IR Type* to EVT (Extended Value Type)
4. **Machine Type Representation** → EVT wraps MVT (Machine Value Type) for target-specific representation
5. **Type Legalization** → LegalizeTypes and language-specific legalization files transform EVT to legal machine types
6. **Code Generation** → Legalized SelectionDAG flows to instruction selection

The answer file includes 25 key files with detailed explanations of how types flow through the entire system, complete with specific line numbers and data structure relationships.

\"text\": \"## LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain\\n\\nThe LLVM type system flows from high-level IR types through SelectionDAG to machine-level types in a multi-stage process:\\n\\n### 1. Type Class Hierarchy (llvm/include/llvm/IR/)\\n\\nThe type system is built on a base Type class (Type.h) with TypeID enum defining all type categories:\\n- **Primitive types**: HalfTyID, FloatTyID, DoubleTyID, VoidTyID, LabelTyID, MetadataTyID\\n- **Derived types**: IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, PointerTyID, StructTyID, ArrayTyID, FixedVectorTyID, ScalableVectorTyID\\n\\nDerivedTypes.h implements the concrete type classes:\\n- **IntegerType**: Represents arbitrary bit-width integers via IntegerType::get(LLVMContext&, unsigned NumBits)\\n- **FunctionType**: Represents function signatures with return and parameter types, created via FunctionType::get(Type*, ArrayRef<Type*>, bool)\\n- **StructType**: Represents structure types (both literal and identified), created via StructType::get() for literal structs and StructType::create() for identified structs\\n- **ArrayType, VectorType, PointerType**: Additional derived types for arrays, vectors, and pointers\\n\\n### 2. Type Context Ownership (llvm/lib/IR/)\\n\\nType uniqueness is managed by LLVMContext (LLVMContext.h) which owns the implementation object (pImpl) of type LLVMContextImpl (LLVMContextImpl.h).\\n\\nLLVMContextImpl maintains type storage maps:\\n- **IntegerTypes**: DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> storing integer types by bit width\\n- **FunctionTypes**: DenseSet<FunctionType*, FunctionTypeKeyInfo> storing function types with uniqueness based on return type, parameters, and varargs\\n- **AnonStructTypes**: DenseSet<StructType*, AnonStructTypeKeyInfo> for anonymous/literal structs, uniqued by element types and packed bit\\n- **NamedStructTypes**: StringMap<StructType*> for identified/named structs\\n- **ArrayTypes, VectorTypes, PointerTypes**: Similar maps for these derived types\\n\\nThe type creation flow (Type.cpp line 318-340) shows IntegerType::get() checking built-in types first, then looking up custom widths in the context's IntegerTypes map, creating new instances if needed via the context's allocator.\\n\\n### 3. SelectionDAG: Intermediate Representation (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nSelectionDAG.h declares the SelectionDAG class which represents the mid-level intermediate representation between IR and target-specific machine code. It operates on SDNode objects (SelectionDAGNodes.h) that form a directed acyclic graph.\\n\\nSelectionDAGBuilder (SelectionDAGBuilder.h/cpp) is responsible for converting IR (with IR types) into SelectionDAG nodes. The builder visits IR instructions and creates corresponding DAG nodes, where each node is annotated with machine types (EVT) rather than IR types.\\n\\n### 4. IR Type to Machine Type Lowering\\n\\nThe critical conversion from IR types to machine types happens through:\\n\\n**TargetLowering::getValueType()**:\\n- Located in TargetLowering.h (line 1740-1742)\\n- Takes a DataLayout and an IR Type* pointer\\n- Returns an EVT (Extended Value Type) representing the machine type\\n- Example usage in FastISel.cpp (line 1470): EVT SrcEVT = TLI.getValueType(DL, I->getOperand(0)->getType())\\n\\n**EVT (Extended Value Type)** - ValueTypes.h:\\n- Represents both simple machine types (through embedded MVT) and complex/extended types\\n- Wraps MVT (Machine Value Type) for simple types like i1, i8, i16, i32, i64, f32, f64\\n- Used throughout SelectionDAG for type-checking and type transformations\\n\\n**MVT (Machine Value Type)** - CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h:\\n- Represents the actual machine-level types supported by the target\\n- Includes integer sizes (i1-i128), floating point types (f16, f32, f64, f128), vector types\\n- This is the minimal type representation used at the machine code level\\n\\n**LLT (Low Level Type)** - CodeGenTypes/LowLevelType.h:\\n- Alternative low-level type representation used by GlobalISel\\n- Simpler than EVT with explicit scalar and vector information\\n\\n### 5. Type Legalization Pipeline (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nAfter SelectionDAG construction, types must be legalized to match target capabilities:\\n\\n**LegalizeTypes** (LegalizeTypes.h/cpp):\\n- Core type legalization framework that transforms EVT to legal machine types\\n- Converts unsupported types to combinations of supported types\\n- DAGTypeLegalizer class drives the process\\n\\n**Type-specific legalization**:\\n- LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp: Handles integer type transformations (promotion, expansion, softening)\\n- LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp: Handles floating-point transformations (softening to integers)\\n- LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp: Handles vector type transformations (splitting, widening, scalarization)\\n- LegalizeDAG.cpp: General DAG operation legalization\\n\\nExample flow (LegalizeTypes.cpp line 432): EVT NewEVT = TLI.getTypeToTransformTo(*DAG.getContext(), OldEVT) transforms an unsupported EVT to a legal equivalent.\\n\\n### Key Data Structure Relationships\\n\\n1. **Type Creation**: User code calls IntegerType::get(Context, 32) \u2192 LLVMContextImpl::IntegerTypes[32] is checked/created\\n2. **DAG Building**: SelectionDAGBuilder visits IR with IR types \u2192 calls TLI.getValueType(Type*) \u2192 EVT\\n3. **Type Legalization**: LegalizeTypes processes EVT \u2192 transforms to legal EVT \u2192 updates SDNode value types\\n4. **Code Generation**: Legalized SelectionDAG with legal MVT types flows to instruction selection and machine code emission\\n\\n### Critical Files Summary\\n\\n**Type Definition Layer**: Type.h, DerivedTypes.h (class hierarchies)\\n**Type Ownership**: LLVMContext.h, LLVMContextImpl.h (storage and uniquing)\\n**Type Implementation**: Type.cpp (factory methods and type creation logic)\\n**DAG Representation**: SelectionDAG.h, SelectionDAGNodes.h (graph structure)\\n**DAG Building**: SelectionDAGBuilder.h/cpp (IR to DAG conversion)\\n**Type Conversion**: TargetLowering.h, ValueTypes.h, MachineValueType.h (type mappings)\\n**Legalization**: LegalizeTypes.h/cpp and language-specific legalization files (type transformation)\"\n}\n",

IR Type to Machine Type Lowering\\n\\nThe critical conversion from IR types to machine types happens through:\\n\\n**TargetLowering::getValueType()**:\\n- Located in TargetLowering.h (line 1740-1742)\\n- Takes a DataLayout and an IR Type* pointer\\n- Returns an EVT (Extended Value Type) representing the machine type\\n- Example usage in FastISel.cpp (line 1470): EVT SrcEVT = TLI.getValueType(DL, I->getOperand(0)->getType())\\n\\n**EVT (Extended Value Type)** - ValueTypes.h:\\n- Represents both simple machine types (through embedded MVT) and complex/extended types\\n- Wraps MVT (Machine Value Type) for simple types like i1, i8, i16, i32, i64, f32, f64\\n- Used throughout SelectionDAG for type-checking and type transformations\\n\\n**MVT (Machine Value Type)** - CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h:\\n- Represents the actual machine-level types supported by the target\\n- Includes integer sizes (i1-i128), floating point types (f16, f32, f64, f128), vector types\\n- This is the minimal type representation used at the machine code level\\n\\n**LLT (Low Level Type)** - CodeGenTypes/LowLevelType.h:\\n- Alternative low-level type representation used by GlobalISel\\n- Simpler than EVT with explicit scalar and vector information\\n\\n### 5. Type Legalization Pipeline (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nAfter SelectionDAG construction, types must be legalized to match target capabilities:\\n\\n**LegalizeTypes** (LegalizeTypes.h/cpp):\\n- Core type legalization framework that transforms EVT to legal machine types\\n- Converts unsupported types to combinations of supported types\\n- DAGTypeLegalizer class drives the process\\n\\n**Type-specific legalization**:\\n- LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp: Handles integer type transformations (promotion, expansion, softening)\\n- LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp: Handles floating-point transformations (softening to integers)\\n- LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp: Handles vector type transformations (splitting, widening, scalarization)\\n- LegalizeDAG.cpp: General DAG operation legalization\\n\\nExample flow (LegalizeTypes.cpp line 432): EVT NewEVT = TLI.getTypeToTransformTo(*DAG.getContext(), OldEVT) transforms an unsupported EVT to a legal equivalent.\\n\\n### Key Data Structure Relationships\\n\\n1. **Type Creation**: User code calls IntegerType::get(Context, 32) \u2192 LLVMContextImpl::IntegerTypes[32] is checked/created\\n2. **DAG Building**: SelectionDAGBuilder visits IR with IR types \u2192 calls TLI.getValueType(Type*) \u2192 EVT\\n3. **Type Legalization**: LegalizeTypes processes EVT \u2192 transforms to legal EVT \u2192 updates SDNode value types\\n4. **Code Generation**: Legalized SelectionDAG with legal MVT types flows to instruction selection and machine code emission\\n\\n### Critical Files Summary\\n\\n**Type Definition Layer**: Type.h, DerivedTypes.h (class hierarchies)\\n**Type Ownership**: LLVMContext.h, LLVMContextImpl.h (storage and uniquing)\\n**Type Implementation**: Type.cpp (factory methods and type creation logic)\\n**DAG Representation**: SelectionDAG.h, SelectionDAGNodes.h (graph structure)\\n**DAG Building**: SelectionDAGBuilder.h/cpp (IR to DAG conversion)\\n**Type Conversion**: TargetLowering.h, ValueTypes.h, MachineValueType.h (type mappings)\\n**Legalization**: LegalizeTypes.h/cpp and language-specific legalization files (type transformation)\"\n}\n",
